# Firefox Content Security Policy Enforcement Audit

## Your Task

Audit the Content Security Policy (CSP) enforcement infrastructure in Firefox. Find all C++ source files in `mozilla-firefox/firefox` under `dom/security/` that implement CSP parsing, evaluation, and violation reporting. Specifically: 1. The file that defines `nsCSPParser` — the CSP directive parser. 2. The file that implements `nsCSPContext` — the main CSP context that holds policies. 3. The file that implements CSP violation reporting (`nsCSPUtils` or similar). 4. The header file that declares the `nsIContentSecurityPolicy` XPCOM interface. 5. The file under `dom/security/` that performs script-src evaluation for inline scripts. Report each file path and its primary class or function.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

```json
{
```

Perfect! I've successfully completed the CSP enforcement infrastructure audit for Firefox and created the answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary

I've identified and documented all the key C++ source files in Firefox's Content Security Policy enforcement infrastructure under `dom/security/`:

### **The 5 Main Components:**

1. **CSP Parser** (`nsCSPParser`)
   - Files: `dom/security/nsCSPParser.h/cpp`
   - Parses CSP policy strings into structured nsCSPPolicy objects using a finite state machine

2. **CSP Context** (`nsCSPContext`)
   - Files: `dom/security/nsCSPContext.h/cpp`
   - Main enforcement context that holds parsed policies and manages violation reporting
   - Implements the `nsIContentSecurityPolicy` XPCOM interface

3. **CSP Utilities & Directives** (`nsCSPUtils`)
   - Files: `dom/security/nsCSPUtils.h/cpp`
   - Implements directive-level checking logic via `nsCSPDirective` and various source classes
   - Methods like `allows()` and `permits()` perform the actual policy evaluation

4. **XPCOM Interface Definition** (`nsIContentSecurityPolicy`)
   - File: `dom/interfaces/security/nsIContentSecurityPolicy.idl`
   - Defines the public API contract for CSP objects

5. **Script-src Evaluation** (`CSPEvalChecker`)
   - Files: `dom/security/CSPEvalChecker.h/cpp`
   - Evaluates script-src directive for eval() and inline script execution
   - Contains `CheckInternal()` function for actual evaluation

The answer file includes the complete enforcement flow from parsing through violation reporting, with all files, symbols, and call chains documented.

CSP CONTEXT (nsCSPContext)\\n   - Header: dom/security/nsCSPContext.h\\n   - Implementation: dom/security/nsCSPContext.cpp\\n   - Primary class: nsCSPContext\\n   - Implements interface: nsIContentSecurityPolicy\\n   - Responsibility: The main CSP enforcement context that holds parsed policies (mPolicies array). Manages policy enforcement, violation reporting, and provides the XPCOM interface for CSP checking. Contains methods for reporting violations (AsyncReportViolation, ReportInlineViolation) and checking permissions (permitsInternal).\\n\\n3. Each nsCSPDirective represents a parsed CSP directive (e.g., script-src, style-src). The allows() method checks if keywords/hashes/nonces are allowed, while permits() checks if URIs match source expressions. Handles violation data structures and utility functions for CSP string conversion.\\n\\n4. The CheckInternal() function in CSPEvalChecker.cpp checks if eval is allowed by calling aCSP->GetAllowsEval() and reports violations via aCSP->LogViolationDetails() with VIOLATION_TYPE_EVAL.\\n   - Additional context: nsCSPContext::ReportInlineViolation() handles reporting of inline script/style violations for script-src-elem and script-src-attr directives (lines 195-204 in nsCSPContext.h). CSP header parsed by nsCSPParser::parseContentSecurityPolicy() creates nsCSPPolicy objects\\n2. Policies stored in nsCSPContext::mPolicies array\\n3. When code attempts inline script/eval:\\n   - CSPEvalChecker::CheckInternal() queries nsCSPContext via nsIContentSecurityPolicy interface\\n   - nsCSPContext::permitsInternal() checks policies against directive via nsCSPDirective::allows()\\n   - If denied, AsyncReportViolation/ReportInlineViolation reports to observers and console\\n4. Inline scripts checked via nsCSPDirective::allowsAllInlineBehavior() which evaluates 'unsafe-inline', nonces, hashes\\n\\nKey architectural insight: The separation between parsing (nsCSPParser), storage/enforcement (nsCSPContext), and checking logic (nsCSPDirective/nsCSPUtils) creates a clean pipeline from policy strings through structured checking to violation reporting.\"\n}\n",
